After all five teams advanced to the second round, No. 12 \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/teams/824\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/824\"\u003eOregon State\u003c/a\u003e punched its ticket to the Sweet 16 first with an 80-70 upset of \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/players/87746\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/87746\"\u003eCade Cunningham\u003c/a\u003e and No. 4 \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/teams/816\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/816\"\u003eOklahoma State\u003c/a\u003e on Sunday. Two weeks ago, the Beavers were on the outside of the field of 68 looking in, but three straight wins in the Pac-12 Tournament saw them nab the conference's automatic berth. They've made the most of it with upsets of both the No. 5 and No. 4 seeds in the Midwest Region, setting up a Sweet 16 matchup with fellow upstart Loyola Chicago. The other four Pac-12 teams take the court Monday, but if Oregon State's success is any indicator, expect the West Coast to be well-represented in the Sweet 16.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eAll Loyola does in March is win, win, win\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs far as winning percentage goes, the most successful NCAA Tournament teams of all time are now Duke and ... \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/teams/590\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/590\"\u003eLoyola Chicago\u003c/a\u003e. The No. 8 seed from the Missouri Valley Conference once again pulled off a stunning upset on the national stage, taking down No. 1 \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/teams/483\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/483\"\u003eIllinois\u003c/a\u003e with a dominant showing Sunday. With the 71-58 victory, the Ramblers improve to 15-5 all time in the tournament, matching the Blue Devils for the best winning percentage during March Madness.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003ePorter Moser's outfit grabbed national attention in 2018 with a run to the Final Four as a No. 11 seed, but the program is no Cinderella this time around. One could argue the committee made the biggest mistake in the field by placing the Ramblers on the No. 8 line. The country's top-ranked defense absolutely smothered Illini All-American \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/players/69644\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/69644\"\u003eAyo Dosunmu\u003c/a\u003e, holding him to nine points on 4-of-10 shooting while forcing him into six turnovers. \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/players/60449\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/60449\"\u003eCameron Krutwig\u003c/a\u003e was an important piece on the 2018 team, but he's a full-fledged star this time around. The senior center finished with 19 points, 12 rebounds, five assists, and four steals.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eRegardless of who the Ramblers play the rest of the way, they'll take the court knowing their defense can shut down any team in the field. On the other side, the top-ranked Illini join No. 2 Ohio State as Big Ten high seeds that suffered early exits. The prevailing thought entering the tournament was that the Big Ten was the nation's top conference, but the weekend's results strongly suggest otherwise.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eHouston alive thanks to insane comeback\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor a large part of Sunday's game versus No. 10 \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/teams/908\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/908\"\u003eRutgers\u003c/a\u003e, it looked like \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/teams/471\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/471\"\u003eHouston\u003c/a\u003e was going to join Ohio State as No. 2 seeds to go home early in the tournament. The Cougars entered the final 4:35 of the contest trailing by nine points. Kelvin Sampson's outfit then launched an outrageous comeback, cutting the deficit to 60-58 with a minute to play. After a Rutgers turnover, it was freshman \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///ncaab/players/85991\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/85991\"\u003eTramon Mark\u003c/a\u003e's turn to play the hero.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"article-segment--embed\"\u003e\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eOH BABY!!! The incredible play denied Rutgers its first trip to the regional semis since 1976 and sees Houston return to the Sweet 16 for the second straight tourney.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eMore double-digit magic for Syracuse\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"article-segment--image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446833/cropped_GettyImages-1308330853.jpg?ts=1616370362\" srcset=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446833/w220xh124_GettyImages-1308330853.jpg?ts=1616370362 220w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446833/w320xh180_GettyImages-1308330853.jpg?ts=1616370362 320w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446833/w640xh360_GettyImages-1308330853.jpg?ts=1616370362 640w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446833/w768xh432_GettyImages-1308330853.jpg?ts=1616370362 768w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446833/w1080xh607_GettyImages-1308330853.jpg?ts=1616370362 1080w\"\u003e\u003cfigcaption class=\"article-segment--image-caption\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"article-segment--image-attribution\"\u003eStacy Revere / Getty Images Sport / Getty\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003eNobody has busted more brackets in the past five tournaments than Jim Boeheim and \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/1056\"\u003eSyracuse\u003c/a\u003e. For the third time in the last five tourneys, the Orange are advancing to the Sweet 16 as a double-digit seed, this time taking down No. 3 West Virginia from the No. 11 slot. According to \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/ESPNStatsInfo/status/1373785841819090945\"\u003eESPN Stats and Info\u003c/a\u003e, Syracuse's 9-2 record is the best winning percentage as a double-digit seed since the tournament began seeding.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Orange, who entered play ranked 64th in the country with 8.4 made 3-pointers per game, torched the Mountaineers defense for seven triples in the first half alone. after halftime to lead 11th-seeded Syracuse past third-seeded West Virginia 75-72 in the NCAA Tournament on Sunday.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eJim Boeheim’s Orange got the better of another legend, Bob Huggins, in the second March Madness meeting between coaches with at least 900 Division I victories. Huggins won No. 900 when West Virginia beat Morehead State in the first round on Friday. Boeheim got his 982nd at Huggins’ expense.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSyracuse (18-9) advanced to face second-seeded Houston or 10th-seeded Rutgers in a Midwest Regional semifinal.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"the-score-article-ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cp\u003eBuddy “Buckets” Boeheim erupted in the second half when he made all but one of his six 3-pointers. He finished 6 of 13 from deep and 8 of 17 overall, and he helped put the game away with three late free throws.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhile deep tournament runs are nothing new for his dad, it’s the first for Buddy, who was a freshman role player when the Orange lost in the opening round two years ago. Now he’s the Orange’s leading scorer and one of college basketball’s most dangerous shooters. He made two straight 3s just after the break, and his jumper and 3 on consecutive possessions put Syracuse ahead 63-59 with 4:55 left.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSean McNeil scored 23 points to lead the Mountaineers (19-10), who last made the Sweet 16 in 2018. That was the fifth time West Virginia got that far under Huggins, who also made the regional semis four times with Cincinnati.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWVU trailed 74-72 with 4 seconds left before Boeheim was fouled at midcourt on an inbounds pass. He made one free throw and missed the second, but Miles McBride traveled after grabbing the rebound.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eJoe Girard III scored all 12 of his points before halftime, steadying the Orange while Boeheim struggled. Quincy Guerrier and Marek Dolezaj also scored 12 each for Syracuse.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBIG PICTURE\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSyracuse: Once again, getting into the tournament as a bubble team did Syracuse no harm. The Orange have advanced to the Sweet 16 each time they’ve been given a double-digit seeding, reaching the Final Four as a 10 in 2016 and the Sweet 16 as an 11 in 2018. That more recent run ended when Boeheim’s bunch lost to Duke and Mike Krzyzewski, the only previous tourney game between 900-win coaches.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWest Virginia: West Virginia: Like many Syracuse opponents, the Mountaineers struggled against the 2-3 zone with poor shooting (37.1%) and turnovers (14). (AP) — Ryan Blaney became the sixth driver to win in six races to start NASCAR's Cup season, surging to the front with nine laps to go after Kyle Larson's dominant performance at Atlanta Motor Speedway fell apart on a fading set of tires Sunday.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLarson easily won the first two stages and led 269 of 325 laps on the 1.54-mile trioval.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut Larson's tires didn't stand up to the punishing track after making his final pit stop with 56 laps to go. Blaney stayed close enough to make his move, hugging the outside wall through the fourth turn and cutting to the inside to pass Larson as they crossed the line in front of the main grandstands.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"the-score-article-ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cp\u003eBlaney pulled away to win by 2.083 seconds in his No. 12 Team Penske Ford.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Gosh, we had a great long-run car all day,” said Blaney, who had to go just as long as Larson on the final set of tires but got much more out of them. “It looked like Kyle was getting loose. It worked out in our favor that there were some long runs at the end.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen it was over, Blaney strolled over to the stands and grabbed the checkered flag, which he handed to a young fan wearing the driver's T-shirt.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt was a bitter loss for Larson, who missed a chance to become 2021's first two-time winner after a victory at Las Vegas two weeks ago.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eStill, he is off to a strong start in his new job at Hendrick Motorsports, less than a year after blurting out a racial slur on the livestream of a late-night video racing game, which cost him his job at Chip Ganassi Racing.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“He was a lot better than me late in the run,” Larson said. “I hate to lead a lot of laps and lose. The car was stupid fast for a long time there. I don't know if we got that much worse or he just got way better.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Cup series returned to the track where the racing world came to a halt a year ago.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn March 2020, Atlanta was the first NASCAR Cup race to be postponed because of the coronavirus pandemic. The series shuttered for more than two months before resuming with major changes to the schedule, including the Atlanta race being held in early June.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis year’s sixth race of the Cup season welcomed a socially distanced crowd of about 20,000 — far below capacity because of the lingering COVID-19 outbreak, but a welcome change from the previous year when no fans were allowed for the makeup race in Atlanta.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Cup racers will return to the 1.54-mile trioval July 11, the first time since 2010 that Atlanta has hosted two races in a season.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eKURT’S CRASH\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eKurt Busch had the look of a contender until the restart to begin the second stage.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs the cars stacked up behind Larson, Busch got bumped from behind by Denny Hamlin and slammed into the outside wall going into turn one.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe No. 1 Chevrolet sustained heavy damage on the right side. Busch was able to nurse his machine back around to pit lane, but he was done for the day.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBusch conceded that Hamlin “didn’t do anything vicious or malicious,” but he was ticked off that the driver of the No. 11 car got so impatient on the restart.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“These are the days that hurt the worst,” said Busch, who finished last in the 39-car field. “It’s a restart. Where are we gonna go, man? Just chill.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eCHASE FLOUNDERS\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt was also a tough day for defending Cup champion and home-state favorite Chase Elliott.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eScheduled to start from the fifth position, he had to take the green from the back of the field after failing multiple inspections before the race.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThen, shortly after a restart to begin the final stage, Elliott’s No. 9 Chevy blew the engine coming off turn four.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith smoke billowing from the back of his car, Elliott made it back to the pits but the crew quickly determined that he wouldn’t be able to continue. The car was pushed to the paddock with a 39th-place finish.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It’s great to be home in Georgia,” Elliott said. “I wish we could’ve had a good result.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUP NEXT\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe series heads to Bristol Motor Speedway next Sunday for the highly anticipated dirt race on the high-banked, half-mile oval in The trio of Alcantara, Lopez, and Sanchez boats electric stuff while regularly throwing in the mid-90s. Realmuto in free agency, even after \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1688\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1688\"\u003eBryce Harper\u003c/a\u003e publically pushed for the club to re-sign the All-Star catcher. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHowever, everything changed after Dombrowski - a two-time World Series-winning executive - took over. Dombrowski maintains a championship-or-bust mentality, which is good news for Philly.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWashington Nationals: Extensions for Juan Soto, Trea Turner?\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Nationals have seen two former franchise cornerstones in Harper and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2908\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2908\"\u003eAnthony Rendon\u003c/a\u003e leave town over the last few years. Vanderbilt star hurler Kumar Rocker is the likely prize come July, and the Pirates will probably get another top pick in 2022 after their futility this year.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSt. Louis Cardinals: Nolan Arenado\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt's not every offseason a club lands a perennial MVP candidate, and acquiring \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2381\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2381\"\u003eArenado\u003c/a\u003e from the Rockies gives the Cardinals just that player. Meanwhile, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/5394\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/5394\"\u003eLuke Weaver\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8470\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8470\"\u003eCaleb Smith\u003c/a\u003e - two pitchers acquired through trades over the past few seasons - have shown ample promise and will anchor the back of the rotation. Toss in a reinforced bullpen, and the Diamondbacks might be quietly very good at suppressing runs.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eColorado Rockies: Trevor Story\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis was Arenado's team. Since the beginning of 2018, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2909\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2909\"\u003eFrancisco Lindor\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/3629\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/3629\"\u003eXander Bogaerts\u003c/a\u003e are the only shortstops worth more WAR than Story, according to \u003ca href=\"https://www.fangraphs.com/leaders.aspx?pos=ss\u0026amp;stats=bat\u0026amp;lg=all\u0026amp;qual=y\u0026amp;type=8\u0026amp;season=2020\u0026amp;month=0\u0026amp;season1=2018\u0026amp;ind=0\u0026amp;team=0\u0026amp;rost=0\u0026amp;age=0\u0026amp;filter=\u0026amp;players=0\u0026amp;startdate=2018-01-01\u0026amp;enddate=2020-12-31\"\u003eFanGraphs\u003c/a\u003e. data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8292\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8292\"\u003eRonald Acuna Jr.\u003c/a\u003e, who's beginning the third season of his eight-year, The trio of Alcantara, Lopez, and Sanchez boats electric stuff while regularly throwing in the mid-90s. The team looked poised to lose J.T. Realmuto in free agency, even after \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1688\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1688\"\u003eBryce Harper\u003c/a\u003e publically pushed for the club to re-sign the All-Star catcher. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHowever, everything changed after Dombrowski - a two-time World Series-winning executive - took over. Realmuto stayed, as did \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2496\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2496\"\u003eDidi Gregorius\u003c/a\u003e, and the franchise added several quality relievers. Dombrowski maintains a championship-or-bust mentality, which is good news for Philly.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWashington Nationals: Extensions for Juan Soto, Trea Turner?\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Nationals have seen two former franchise cornerstones in Harper and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2908\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2908\"\u003eAnthony Rendon\u003c/a\u003e leave town over the last few years. Washington can't afford to let \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8271\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8271\"\u003eSoto\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/4814\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/4814\"\u003eTurner\u003c/a\u003e test the open market, even with both players still arbitration-eligible for years. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe club has discussed extensions with its two homegrown stars, but how might the new deals be structured? How much could the agreements cost? Losing \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2916\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2916\"\u003eTrevor Bauer\u003c/a\u003e hurts, but Cincinnati's rotation remains relatively strong as long as \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/3012\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/3012\"\u003eSonny Gray\u003c/a\u003e's injury doesn't keep him sidelined for an extended period. Meanwhile, the lineup is very complete, with \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8159\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8159\"\u003eNick Senzel\u003c/a\u003e hopefully taking a step forward. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eMaybe the Reds can actually put it together while facing lowered expectations and a worse division.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMilwaukee Brewers: Dominant relievers\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTwo of the nastiest relievers in the majors call Milwaukee home, as \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/5307\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/5307\"\u003eJosh Hader\u003c/a\u003e and Devin Williams produce must-watch TV with their overpowering stuff. The former has struck out 380 hitters over 172 career appearances, while the latter recorded a stunning 17.7 K/9 in 2020, resulting in Williams getting NL Rookie of the Year honors.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Brewers can win a lot of close games with the duo locking down the final innings.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePittsburgh Pirates: Drafting No. 1\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt's going to be a very long season for the Pirates. The club is expected to finish with one of the lowest win totals after trading away veteran talent over the winter and committing to a full rebuild. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003ePittsburgh was awful in 2020, too, leading to holding the first pick in 2021. Vanderbilt star hurler Kumar Rocker is the likely prize come July, and the Pirates will probably get another top pick in 2022 after their futility this year.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSt. Louis Cardinals: Nolan Arenado\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt's not every offseason a club lands a perennial MVP candidate, and acquiring \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2381\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2381\"\u003eArenado\u003c/a\u003e from the Rockies gives the Cardinals just that player. The five-time All-Star improves St. Louis in every way imaginable, with the all-around difference-maker instantly lifting the Cardinals to being NL Central favorites.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe 29-year-old has won four Silver Sluggers thanks to a career .890 OPS with 235 homers and 760 RBIs. Arenado has also picked up eight Gold Gloves and four Platinum Gloves for his work at the hot corner.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"article-segment--image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/445532/cropped_GettyImages-1231675740.jpg?ts=1615752402\" srcset=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/445532/w220xh124_GettyImages-1231675740.jpg?ts=1615752402 220w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/445532/w320xh180_GettyImages-1231675740.jpg?ts=1615752402 320w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/445532/w640xh360_GettyImages-1231675740.jpg?ts=1615752402 640w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/445532/w768xh432_GettyImages-1231675740.jpg?ts=1615752402 768w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/445532/w1080xh607_GettyImages-1231675740.jpg?ts=1615752402 1080w\"\u003e\u003cfigcaption class=\"article-segment--image-caption\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"article-segment--image-attribution\"\u003eMatt Thomas/San Diego Padres / Getty Images Sport / Getty\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNL West\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eArizona Diamondbacks: The rotation\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Diamondbacks seem to hold the most legitimate claim to third place in the division, and they could challenge for a wild-card spot if everything breaks right and the NL East is worse than expected.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat quest will start with the rotation. \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1261\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1261\"\u003eMadison Bumgarner\u003c/a\u003e is looking to bounce back from a miserable debut season with Arizona when he recorded his first win on the last day of the campaign, and Zac Gallen will be in his first truly full season as the ace of the staff. Meanwhile, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/5394\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/5394\"\u003eLuke Weaver\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8470\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8470\"\u003eCaleb Smith\u003c/a\u003e - two pitchers acquired through trades over the past few seasons - have shown ample promise and will anchor the back of the rotation. If \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/4059\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/4059\"\u003eMerrill Kelly\u003c/a\u003e falters in the fifth spot, one of \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/10565\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/10565\"\u003eTaylor Widener\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/9521\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/9521\"\u003eJon Duplantier\u003c/a\u003e, or \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8127\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8127\"\u003eAlex Young\u003c/a\u003e is ready to step in for Arizona. Toss in a reinforced bullpen, and the Diamondbacks might be quietly very good at suppressing runs.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eColorado Rockies: Trevor Story\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis was Arenado's team. Now \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/4232\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/4232\"\u003eStory\u003c/a\u003e will lead the Rockies for at least one more season, and he's more than deserving of that spotlight. Since the beginning of 2018, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2909\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2909\"\u003eFrancisco Lindor\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/3629\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/3629\"\u003eXander Bogaerts\u003c/a\u003e are the only shortstops worth more WAR than Story, according to \u003ca href=\"https://www.fangraphs.com/leaders.aspx?pos=ss\u0026amp;stats=bat\u0026amp;lg=all\u0026amp;qual=y\u0026amp;type=8\u0026amp;season=2020\u0026amp;month=0\u0026amp;season1=2018\u0026amp;ind=0\u0026amp;team=0\u0026amp;rost=0\u0026amp;age=0\u0026amp;filter=\u0026amp;players=0\u0026amp;startdate=2018-01-01\u0026amp;enddate=2020-12-31\"\u003eFanGraphs\u003c/a\u003e. Story could walk away this coming winter, and he might even be traded midseason. But Rockies fans should still appreciate him while he's in Colorado.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd when Story does leave, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/5397\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/5397\"\u003eBrendan Rodgers\u003c/a\u003e - who will miss the first month of the season - should take the reins at shortstop.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLos Angeles Dodgers: Forging a dynasty\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDodgers fans have been waiting five years for this, and it's time to start a dynasty now that the championship drought is over. The Cubs and Houston Astros failed, but neither of those teams added the reigning NL Cy Young winner to a group that already includes \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/4184\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/4184\"\u003eMookie Betts\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/4899\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/4899\"\u003eCody Bellinger\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/945\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/945\"\u003eClayton Kershaw\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8193\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8193\"\u003eWalker Buehler\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/3924\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/3924\"\u003eCorey Seager\u003c/a\u003e. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe mission to be the first to repeat since the New York Yankees last millennium is beginning, and there's a very legitimate case that this team is even better than in 2020, when the Dodgers played at a 116-win pace.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSan Diego Padres: Literally everything\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhat's not to love about this team? The brown and yellow jerseys are making a long-awaited return. \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/8286\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/8286\"\u003eFernando Tatis Jr.\u003c/a\u003e is already the league's most exciting player and the likely eventual heir to \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1674\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1674\"\u003eMike Trout\u003c/a\u003e's throne as the best overall star (if there is one), and now he's in San Diego through 2034. \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/5351\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/5351\"\u003eBlake Snell\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/2901\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/2901\"\u003eYu Darvish\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/5369\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/5369\"\u003eJoe Musgrove\u003c/a\u003e were added to the rotation. The bullpen is one of the league's best. And San Diego is slated for 19 games against the reigning champs in what should be appointment viewing for every MLB fan.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSan Francisco Giants: The unofficial beginning of the turnaround\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAside from \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1259\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1259\"\u003eBuster Posey\u003c/a\u003e, the key pieces of the Giants' dynasty are pretty much gone. Bumgarner is now with the division-rival Diamondbacks, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1249\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1249\"\u003ePablo Sandoval\u003c/a\u003e is playing for the Braves, and Tim Lincecum is, well, doing Tim Lincecum things. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut the rebuild Farhan Zaidi is orchestrating will reach its next stage this season. \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/760\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/760\"\u003eJohnny Cueto\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1834\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1834\"\u003eBrandon Crawford\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca data-in-app-uri=\"thescore:///mlb/players/1658\" href=\"https://www.thescore.com/mlb/players/1658\"\u003eBrandon Belt\u003c/a\u003e are all set to come off the books at the end of the year, clearing roughly $54.5 million of payroll. Even Posey's $22-million team option might not be picked up. There's still work to be done, and it begins in earnest The Golden Eagles became the ninth 15-seed all time to win an NCAA Tournament game.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"the-score-article-ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e Despite an inconsistent summit league campaign that saw the school finish fourth, the Golden Eagles caught fire in their conference tournament and advanced to March Madness. Led by Abmas - the nation's leading scorer at 24.5 points per game - Oral Roberts gave Oklahoma State and Arkansas a scare back in December, showing its bracket-breaking ability.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because 15-seeds don't come built like this often. Many times, major underdogs attempt to slow the game down and wear out their opponents, but Oral Roberts never stops running and makes more threes than any school in the country. If you're looking to back a team coming off a monumental upset that isn't afraid of the big stage, \"Midcourt\" Abmas and the Golden Eagles are the way to go.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 12 Oregon State\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"article-segment--image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/cropped_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582\" srcset=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w220xh124_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 220w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w320xh180_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 320w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w640xh360_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 640w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w768xh432_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 768w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w1080xh607_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 1080w\"\u003e\u003cfigcaption class=\"article-segment--image-caption\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"article-segment--image-attribution\"\u003eJoe Robbins/NCAA Photos / NCAA Photos / Getty\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/824\"\u003eOregon State\u003c/a\u003e led wire-to-wire to defeat Tennessee 70-56 thanks to 10 made threes and a stifling defense. The victory marked the Beavers' first NCAA Tournament win since 1982.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e After brutal non-conference performances that saw Oregon State lose to Wyoming and Portland - ranked 162nd and 327th in the NET, respectively - the Beavers turned it on down the stretch. They won six of their last seven to win the Pac-12 Tournament for the first time ever.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e While Oregon State may not have a superstar leading the way, it gets something different from everyone in the rotation. Whether it's \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/62168\"\u003eEthan Thompson\u003c/a\u003e's drives, \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/78023\"\u003eJarod Lucas\u003c/a\u003e' sharpshooting, or \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/70667\"\u003eWarith Alatishe\u003c/a\u003e's defense, each Beaver knows their role and doesn't try to do too much. This well-balanced squad is nearing uncharted territory in Oregon State's modern-day history.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 11 Syracuse\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64\u003c/strong\u003e: \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/1056\"\u003eSyracuse\u003c/a\u003e handled San Diego State 78-62 behind \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/70916\"\u003eBuddy Boeheim\u003c/a\u003e's 30 points and seven 3-pointers. Buddy's dad, coach Jim Boeheim became the first men's coach to win an NCAA Tournament game in \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/CBBonFOX/status/1373117686620692488\"\u003esix different decades\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e The Orange had an underwhelming regular season which saw them finish eighth in a below-average ACC and without a victory against the top 30 in the NET rankings. Still, it was assumed coach Boeheim's bunch would turn it on for March Madness, and that's exactly what happened in their blowout victory over the Aztecs.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because this Syracuse squad seems to embrace the challenge of being a double-digit seed. After making the Final Four as a 10-seed in 2016, the Orange made the Sweet Sixteen as an 11 in 2018, and are at it again this year. If you're the type of person who likes to save your best for last, this surging Syracuse group is a great team to get behind.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 13 North Texas\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"article-segment--image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446633/cropped_GettyImages-1231819186.jpg?ts=1616282686\" srcset=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446633/w220xh124_GettyImages-1231819186.jpg?ts=1616282686 220w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446633/w320xh180_GettyImages-1231819186.jpg?ts=1616282686 320w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446633/w640xh360_GettyImages-1231819186.jpg?ts=1616282686 640w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446633/w768xh432_GettyImages-1231819186.jpg?ts=1616282686 768w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446633/w1080xh607_GettyImages-1231819186.jpg?ts=1616282686 1080w\"\u003e\u003cfigcaption class=\"article-segment--image-caption\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"article-segment--image-attribution\"\u003eJamie Schwaberow / NCAA Photos / Getty\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/772\"\u003eNorth Texas\u003c/a\u003e upset Purdue 78-69 in overtime behind \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/76346\"\u003eJavion Hamlet\u003c/a\u003e's 24 points, 12 rebounds, and five assists. The win marked the Mean Green's first-ever NCAA Tournament victory.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e Just three weeks ago, North Texas was 13-9 and entered its conference tournament as the sixth seed. Now, after winning four games in as many days to win the C-USA title and take down Purdue, the Mean Green are one of the hottest teams in the country.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because this squad plays extremely hard and brings energy each game. The Mean Green are the definition of scrappy, and despite not having elite size, continue to find ways to pull out victories. Watching North Texas work hard on the court makes you want to finish those chores you've been putting off all week.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 10 Rutgers\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/908\"\u003eRutgers\u003c/a\u003e held on to beat Clemson 60-56 in a back-and-forth affair. The Scarlet Knights had four scorers in double figures to give the school its first March Madness win since 1983.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e This season was a roller coaster for Rutgers. After starting the campaign 7-1 and being ranked 11 in the AP Poll, it lost five straight, then won four in a row, and finally settled somewhere near the middle. Leading scorer \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/70554\"\u003eRon Harper Jr.\u003c/a\u003e's effectiveness was a key factor, as he averaged 17.2 points per game in wins, and only 12.5 in losses.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because Rutgers has been the laughing stock of modern-day Power 5 basketball. Not only did the Scarlet Knights win their first NCAA Tournament game in 38 years, but they've been shut out of the big dance entirely since 1991. Any further success this season would reach territory untouched since the mid-70s, so if you're interested in reliving the good old days, Rutgers is the team to action.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 15 Oral Roberts\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/822\"\u003eOral Roberts\u003c/a\u003e beat Ohio State 75-72 in overtime behind 59 combined points from stars \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/79213\"\u003eMax Abmas\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/69968\"\u003eKevin Obanor\u003c/a\u003e. The Golden Eagles became the ninth 15-seed all time to win an NCAA Tournament game.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"the-score-article-ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e Despite an inconsistent summit league campaign that saw the school finish fourth, the Golden Eagles caught fire in their conference tournament and advanced to March Madness. Led by Abmas - the nation's leading scorer at 24.5 points per game - Oral Roberts gave Oklahoma State and Arkansas a scare back in December, showing its bracket-breaking ability.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because 15-seeds don't come built like this often. Many times, major underdogs attempt to slow the game down and wear out their opponents, but Oral Roberts never stops running and makes more threes than any school in the country. If you're looking to back a team coming off a monumental upset that isn't afraid of the big stage, \"Midcourt\" Abmas and the Golden Eagles are the way to go.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 12 Oregon State\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"article-segment--image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/cropped_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582\" srcset=\"https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w220xh124_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 220w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w320xh180_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 320w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w640xh360_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 640w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w768xh432_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 768w, https://assets-cms.thescore.com/uploads/image/file/446631/w1080xh607_GettyImages-1308008413.jpg?ts=1616282582 1080w\"\u003e\u003cfigcaption class=\"article-segment--image-caption\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"article-segment--image-attribution\"\u003eJoe Robbins/NCAA Photos / NCAA Photos / Getty\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/824\"\u003eOregon State\u003c/a\u003e led wire-to-wire to defeat Tennessee 70-56 thanks to 10 made threes and a stifling defense. The victory marked the Beavers' first NCAA Tournament win since 1982.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e After brutal non-conference performances that saw Oregon State lose to Wyoming and Portland - ranked 162nd and 327th in the NET, respectively - the Beavers turned it on down the stretch. They won six of their last seven to win the Pac-12 Tournament for the first time ever.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e While Oregon State may not have a superstar leading the way, it gets something different from everyone in the rotation. This well-balanced squad is nearing uncharted territory in Oregon State's modern-day history.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 11 Syracuse\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64\u003c/strong\u003e: \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/1056\"\u003eSyracuse\u003c/a\u003e handled San Diego State 78-62 behind \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/70916\"\u003eBuddy Boeheim\u003c/a\u003e's 30 points and seven 3-pointers. Buddy's dad, coach Jim Boeheim became the first men's coach to win an NCAA Tournament game in \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/CBBonFOX/status/1373117686620692488\"\u003esix different decades\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e The Orange had an underwhelming regular season which saw them finish eighth in a below-average ACC and without a victory against the top 30 in the NET rankings. Still, it was assumed coach Boeheim's bunch would turn it on for March Madness, and that's exactly what happened in their blowout victory over the Aztecs.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because this Syracuse squad seems to embrace the challenge of being a double-digit seed. After making the Final Four as a 10-seed in 2016, the Orange made the Sweet Sixteen as an 11 in 2018, and are at it again this year. The win marked the Mean Green's first-ever NCAA Tournament victory.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e Just three weeks ago, North Texas was 13-9 and entered its conference tournament as the sixth seed. Now, after winning four games in as many days to win the C-USA title and take down Purdue, the Mean Green are one of the hottest teams in the country.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because this squad plays extremely hard and brings energy each game. The Mean Green are the definition of scrappy, and despite not having elite size, continue to find ways to pull out victories. Watching North Texas work hard on the court makes you want to finish those chores you've been putting off all week.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003eNo. 10 Rutgers\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRound of 64:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/teams/908\"\u003eRutgers\u003c/a\u003e held on to beat Clemson 60-56 in a back-and-forth affair. The Scarlet Knights had four scorers in double figures to give the school its first March Madness win since 1983.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeason resume:\u003c/strong\u003e This season was a roller coaster for Rutgers. After starting the campaign 7-1 and being ranked 11 in the AP Poll, it lost five straight, then won four in a row, and finally settled somewhere near the middle. Leading scorer \u003ca href=\"https://www.thescore.com/ncaab/players/70554\"\u003eRon Harper Jr.\u003c/a\u003e's effectiveness was a key factor, as he averaged 17.2 points per game in wins, and only 12.5 in losses.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy you should root for them:\u003c/strong\u003e Because Rutgers has been the laughing stock of modern-day Power 5 basketball. Not only did the Scarlet Knights win their first NCAA Tournament game in 38 years, but they've been shut out of the big dance entirely since 1991. Any further success this season would reach territory untouched since the mid-70s, so if you're interested in reliving the good old days, Rutgers is the team to
